ARIE vol.052, 1929-1930


A. List of copper-plates examined during the year 1929-30.
1
Placement
The Trustee of the Sundara-rāja-Perumāḷ temple atAḻagarkōyil, Madura taluk,Madura district.
Year
Sētupati
King
Vijayaraghunātha-Sētupati-dēva.
Date
Śaka 1634, Nan-dana, Dakshiṇā-yana, Grīshma,Āshāḍha, ba.amāvāsyā. Tues-day, Pushya.
Language and Script
Tamil
Remarks
States that Muttuvayiravanāthadēva,son of Kaḍambattēvar who wasthe elder brother of the king andwas residing at Uttarakōśamaṅgai,remitted half of the revenue fromthe villages Āykkuḍi and Śunda-ṉāvūr which belonged to Tiruveṅ-kaṭāchārya, son of Tirumalaiyāṇḍa-Tiruveṅkaṭāchārya, for the ex-penses of feeding in the temple ofAḻagar and for digging a tankbetween the temple and Appaṉ-Tirupati. The king calls him-self ‘the lord of Tēvainagar(Rāmēśvaram)’ and had the ‘Hanu-mān-banner’.
2
Placement
Mr. Dupati Papayya, Priestof the Śiva temple at Goṭṭi-mukkala. Palnad taluk,Guntur district.
Year
…
King
…
Date
Śaka 1725, Rudhi-rōdgāri, Mārga,śu. 5, Sunday.
Language and Script
Telugu
Remarks
Registers the varshāśana-patrikāgiven by the 102 nagaras of Goṭṭi-mukkala for the maintenance ofworship and lamps in the temple ofUttarēśvarasvāmin at the village,and specifies the rates of tolls to belevied upon various articles ofmerchandise passing through theghat (at that place).

B. Stone inscriptions copied during the year 1929-30.

Telugu
Remarks

Records that at the request of Pichchaṉ Śīvallavaṉ ofTirunelvēli in Kīḻvēmba-nāḍu, the king, while seated inhis palace at Māḍakkuḷam to the east of Madura, orderedthat Kaṭṭāṇimaṅgalam should henceforth be calledVikramapāṇḍya-chaturvēdimaṅgalam. Mention is madeof 64 Brahmans well-versed in the Vēdas and the Śāstras, settled here and paying the kaḍamai to the temple.

Mentions the Mahājanasof the Brahmapuri of the god and the araṇi-guttiga(tenant) of the garden, Bammaṇa, who was to supply theflower-garlands and vegetables required for the temple.The seṭṭiguttas and nakharas of Muttage contributedbdellium, etc., required for the festivals of the deity,while the Mahājanas granted one oil-mill together withthe site on which it stood.

Placement

King
Bhujabalamalladēva (i.e., Bijjala)
Date
10th year, Pārthiva,Śrāvaṇa, ba. 12,Thursday, Vyatīpāta.
Language and Script
Kannaḍa (prose & verse)
Remarks
Records the gift of the hejjuṅka and other taxes of Muttagemade to the temple of Rāmēśvaradēva at the agrahāra ofMuttage, by Rājādhyaksha, Suṅkavergaḍe Dāsimayya-Nāyaka, son of Sēnādhipati Śrikaraṇa Haridēvayya-Daṇḍanāyaka of the Ātrēya-gōtra. The gift was madeinto the hands of Rudraśakti-muni. Later on the prabhuGōvinda, son of Bāchirāja, gave some land to the sametemple.

Language and Script
Kannaḍa
Remarks
Records the gifts of lands, oil, etc., made by Sīripayya,the son of Hariyanṇa of Hagaraṭṭage, who belonged tothe Vā[ji]-vaṁśa and was the Śrīkaraṇa of the Mahāpra-dhāna Rāyadaṇḍādhiśa Sarvādhikāri, Chauḍi-Śeṭṭi whowas governing over the Two [Beḷu ?]valas, Banavāsi-Pāṇḍyanāḍu, Hānuṁ[gal-Pāṇḍināḍu], Tardavāḍi, etc.,countries while the latter's maternal uncle Raṅgarasawas governing the villages of Sālavāḍige, Bāgavāḍi etc.The gift was made for the benefit of the temple ofGōpāladēva and of the sixteen Mahājanas attached to thedeity. Records also gifts of lands made to the temples ofLakshmaṇēśvaradēva and Bhāskaradēva.
115
Placement
Broken slab standing near theentrance to the Masjid.
Year
…
King
…
Date
…
Language and Script
Kannaḍa (verse)
Remarks
This is a composite record registering several facts andgifts. Praises king Śubhatuṅgavallabha born in theRāshṭrakūṭa line, and Kannara and Akālavarsha, whichwere respectively the name and surname of Kṛishṇa II,who is also called Kṛishṇarāja in the inscription. Statesthat his subordinate Horeyama-Sāmanta built a templeof Śiva at Sālavaḍige and that king Śubhatuṅga grantedsome land to it. Subsequently, when this temple fellinto ruin a Śivayati named Mūṟudēvimuni renovated itand consecrated in it the two deities of Siddhēśvara andPāpavināśadēva, to which land was given in the time ofking Jagadēkamalla of the Chālukya line descended fromking Nūrmaḍi-Tailapa, by Chikabbe, the daughter of acertain Mūliga Mākamayya. Gifts made by the fourchief Prabhus or Ūroḍeyas of Sāḷavāḍige who belonged tothe Ātrēya-gōtra and Vāji-vaṁśa, by the residents of thevillage and by the Three-Hundred Paṭṭasaligas are alsorecorded.

Records the gifts of lands, etc. made by Adhikāri Saṇṇu-Nāyaru and the several people of Bailūr, to a certainNārāyaṇa-Bhaṭṭa for expounding the Purāṇas daily inthe temple of Maḍakēśvara, and also the gifts made tothe same donee by Surēśvara-Śrīpāda and the severalpeople, for expounding the Purāṇas on the 30 days ofthe month of Śrāvaṇa in the maṭha of the Śrīpāda.
